AAC)</a></li></ul>\n</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Website</th><td>\n<span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://bbc.co.uk/radio3">BBC Radio 3</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>BBC Radio 3</b> is a British radio station operated by the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>.  Its output centres on <a href="/wiki/Classical_music" title="Classical music">classical music</a> and <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">opera</a>, but <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_music" title="World music">world music</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radio_drama" title="Radio drama">drama</a>, <a href="/wiki/High_culture" title="High culture">culture</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_arts" title="The arts">the arts</a> also feature.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Radio_3_Service_Licence_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Radio_3_Service_Licence-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The station is the world\'s most significant commissioner of new music,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> and through its <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_3_New_Generation_Artists_scheme" title="BBC Radio 3 New Generation Artists scheme">New Generation Artists scheme</a> promotes young musicians of all nationalities.<sup id="cite_ref-NGA_Radio3_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NGA_Radio3-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The station broadcasts the <a href="/wiki/The_Proms" title="The Proms">BBC Proms</a> concerts, live and in full, each summer in addition to performances by the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Orchestras_and_Singers" title="BBC Orchestras and Singers">BBC Orchestras and Singers</a>. There are regular productions of both classic plays and newly commissioned drama.\n</p><p>Radio 3 won the Sony <a href="/wiki/Radio_Academy" title="Radio Academy">Radio Academy</a> UK Station of the Year Gold Award for 2009<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and was nominated again in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="tocnumber">3.6</span> <span class="toctext"><i>Pied Piper</i></span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Radio_3_in_Concert"><span class="tocnumber">3.7</span> <span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_BBC_Radio_3" title="Timeline of BBC Radio 3">Timeline of BBC Radio 3</a></div>\n<p>Radio 3 is the successor station to the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Third_Programme" title="BBC Third Programme">BBC Third Programme</a> which began broadcasting on 29 September 1946.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The name Radio 3 was adopted on 30 September 1967 when the BBC launched its first pop music station, <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1" title="BBC Radio 1">Radio 1</a><sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>247</span></sup> and rebranded its national radio channels as Radio 1, <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_2" title="BBC Radio 2">Radio 2</a> (formerly the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Light_Programme" title="BBC Light Programme">Light Programme</a>), Radio 3, and <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_4" title="BBC Radio 4">Radio 4</a> (formerly the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Home_Service" title="BBC Home Service">Home Service</a>).\n</p><p>Radio 3 was the overall label applied to the collection of services which had until then gone under the umbrella title of the Third Network, namely:\n</p>\n<ul><li>the Third Programme proper (as launched in 1946, an evenings-only offering of demanding cultural fare, both musical and spoken)</li>\n<li>the Music Programme (a daytime service of classical music)</li>\n<li>sports coverage (chiefly on Saturday afternoons) and adult educational programming in the early part of weekday evenings (known as Network Three).</li></ul>\n<p>All these strands, including the Third Programme, kept their separate identities within Radio 3 until 4 April 1970, when there was a further reorganisation following the introduction of the structural changes which had been outlined the previous year in the BBC document <i>Broadcasting in the Seventies</i>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcasting_in_the_Seventies"><i>Broadcasting in the Seventies</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Broadcasting in the Seventies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 10 July 1969 the BBC published its plans for radio and television in a policy document entitled <i>Broadcasting in the Seventies</i>. Later described in 2002 by <a href="/wiki/Jenny_Abramsky" title="Jenny Abramsky">Jenny Abramsky</a>, Head of Radio and Music, as "the most controversial document ever produced by radio",<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> the document outlined each station\'s target audience and what content should be broadcast on each channel. This concept went against the earlier methods laid out by the BBC\'s first Director General <a href="/wiki/John_Reith,_1st_Baron_Reith" title="John Reith, 1st Baron Reith">John Reith</a> and caused controversy at the time, despite laying out the radio structure that is recognisable today.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the time of the review, Radio 3 faced several problems. An early option to cut costs, required under the proposals, was to reduce the number of networks from four to three, so that Radio 3 would not broadcast during the day and would use the frequencies of either Radio 1 or 2 as the two stations would merge content. However "Day-time serious music would be the casualty" of these proposals and caused some controversy.<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>249</span></sup> A further rumour was expressed that Radio 3 could be closed altogether as a strong statistical case existed against the station according to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>251</span></sup> However, the Director-General, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Curran_(broadcaster)" title="Charles Curran (broadcaster)">Charles Curran</a>, publicly denied this as "quite contradictory to the aim of the BBC, which is to provide a comprehensive radio service".<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>251</span></sup> Curran had earlier dismissed any suggestion that Radio 3\'s small audience was a consideration: "What is decisive is whether there is a worthwhile audience, and I mean by worthwhile an audience which will get an enormous satisfaction out of it."<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>251</span></sup>\n</p><p>As a result of <i>Broadcasting in the Seventies</i>, factual content, including documentaries and current affairs, were moved to <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_4" title="BBC Radio 4">BBC Radio 4</a> and the separate titled strands were abolished. The document stated that Radio 3 was to have "a larger output of standard classical music" but with "some element in the evening of cultural speech programmes \xe2\x80\x93 poetry, plays".<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>253</span></sup> Equally, questions were being asked by the poet <a href="/wiki/Peter_Porter_(poet)" title="Peter Porter (poet)">Peter Porter</a> about whether other spoken content, for example poetry, would remain on the station. These concerns also led to the composer <a href="/wiki/Peter_Maxwell_Davies" title="Peter Maxwell Davies">Peter Maxwell Davies</a> and the music critic <a href="/wiki/Edward_Greenfield" title="Edward Greenfield">Edward Greenfield</a> to fear that "people would lose the mix of cultural experiences which expanded intellectual horizons".<sup id="cite_ref-RT4-4-70_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT4-4-70-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> However, Radio 3 controller <a href="/wiki/P._H._Newby" title="P. H. Newby">Howard Newby</a> reassured these concerns by replying that only the coverage of political and economic affairs would be passed to Radio 4: Radio 3 would keep drama, poetry, and talks by scientists, philosophers and historians.<sup id="cite_ref-RT4-4-70_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT4-4-70-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <i>Broadcasting in the Seventies</i> report also proposed a large cutback in the number and size of the BBC\'s orchestras. In September 1969, a distinguished campaign group entitled the Campaign for Better Broadcasting was formed to protest, with the backing of <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Boult" title="Adrian Boult">Sir Adrian Boult</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Miller" title="Jonathan Miller">Jonathan Miller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Moore" title="Henry Moore">Henry Moore</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Melly" title="George Melly">George Melly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The campaign objected to "the dismantling of the Third Programme by cutting down its spoken word content from fourteen hours a week to six"  and "segregating programmes into classes".<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Mention of the campaign even reached debate in the House of Commons.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="The_.27arts.27_controllers"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_\'arts\'_controllers">The \'arts\' controllers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: The &#039;arts&#039; controllers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>From the launch until 1987, the controllers of Radio 3 showed preferences towards speech and arts programming as opposed to focus on classical music and the Proms. The first controller, Newby, made little contribution to the station, focusing on the transition from the Third programme to Radio 3 and as a result of the <i>Broadcasting in the Seventies</i> report.\n</p><p>The second controller, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hearst" title="Stephen Hearst">Stephen Hearst</a> who assumed the role in 1972, was different. As Hearst had previously been head of television arts features<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> his appointment was seen with scepticism among the staff who viewed him as a populariser.<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>269</span></sup> According to Hearst when interviewed for <a href="/wiki/Humphrey_Carpenter" title="Humphrey Carpenter">Humphrey Carpenter</a>\'s book, the main rival candidate for controller <a href="/wiki/Martin_Esslin" title="Martin Esslin">Martin Esslin</a>, head of Radio Drama, had said to the interviewing panel that audience figures should play no part in the decision making process over programming.<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>268</span></sup> Hearst said he responded to the same question about this issue by commenting that as the station was financed by public money it needed to consider the size of its audience \xe2\x80\x93 there was a minimum viable figure but this could be increased with "a lively style of broadcasting",<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>268</span></sup>\n</p><p>Hearst attempted to make the content of the channel more accessible to a wider audience, but his efforts, which included the evening drivetime programme <i>Homeward Bound</i> and Sunday phone-in request programme <i>Your Concert Choice</i> (the former an uninterrupted sequence of musical items identified only at the end of the programme; the latter a resurrection from the old <a href="/wiki/Home_Service" title="Home Service">Home Service</a>), were criticised.<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>289, 296</span></sup> However, during this time the long running arts discussion programme <i>Critics\' Forum</i> was launched<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>290</span></sup> as well as themed evenings and programmes of miscellaneous music including <i>Sounds Interesting</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1978, <a href="/wiki/Ian_McIntyre" title="Ian McIntyre">Ian McIntyre</a> took over as controller of Radio 3 but quickly faced uncomfortable relationships between departments. At approximately the same time <a href="/wiki/Aubrey_Singer" title="Aubrey Singer">Aubrey Singer</a> became Managing Director of Radio and began to make programming on the station more populist in a drive to retain listeners in face of possible competition from competitors using a "streamed format".<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>304</span></sup> An example of this is the replacement of <i>Homeward Bound</i> in 1980 with an extended, presenter-driven programme called <i>Mainly for Pleasure</i>. The same year an internal paper recommended the disbandment of several of the BBC\'s orchestras and of the Music Division, resulting in low morale and <a href="/wiki/Strike_action" title="Strike action">industrial action</a> by musicians that delayed the start of the Proms.<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>306\xe2\x80\x93307</span></sup> Senior management was also getting dissatisfied with listening figures leading to the Director-General <a href="/wiki/Alasdair_Milne" title="Alasdair Milne">Alasdair Milne</a> to suggest that presentation style was "too stodgy and old-fashioned".<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>313</span></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="The_.27music.27_controllers"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_\'music\'_controllers">The \'music\' controllers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: The &#039;music&#039; controllers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1987 the positions of Controller of Music and Controller of Radio 3 were merged, and with it the operation of the Proms, under the former Music Controller <a href="/wiki/John_Drummond_(arts_administrator)" title="John Drummond (arts administrator)">John Drummond</a>. Drummond, like Hearst, believed that the music programmes\' presentation was too stiff and formal<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>326</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> and he therefore encouraged announcers to be more natural and enthusiastic. Repeats of classic drama performances by the likes of <a href="/wiki/John_Gielgud" title="John Gielgud">John Gielgud</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Scofield" title="Paul Scofield">Paul Scofield</a> were also included because, in his view, newer drama was "gloomy and pretentious".<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> He also introduced features and celebrations of the anniversaries of famous figures including <a href="/wiki/William_Glock" title="William Glock">William Glock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Tippett" title="Michael Tippett">Michael Tippett</a> and <a href="/wiki/Isaiah_Berlin" title="Isaiah Berlin">Isaiah Berlin</a>. Drummond also introduced the show <i><a href="/wiki/Mixing_It" title="Mixing It">Mixing It</a></i> which targeted the music genres that fell between Radios 1 and 3, often seen as a precursor to the programme <i><a href="/wiki/Late_Junction" title="Late Junction">Late Junction</a></i>.\n</p><p>During Drummond\'s time, Radio 3 also began to experiment with outside broadcasts including an ambitious Berlin Weekend to mark the <a href="/wiki/German_Reunification" class="mw-redirect" title="German Reunification">reunification of Germany</a> in 1990 and a much praised weekend of programming that was broadcast from London and <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis-St_Paul" class="mw-redirect" title="Minneapolis-St Paul">Minneapolis-St Paul</a> \xe2\x80\x93 creating broadcasting history by being the first time a whole weekend had been transmitted "live from another continent".<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>331</span></sup> However, Drummond complained about the former that "not one single senior person in the BBC had listened to any part of it",<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>331</span></sup> reflecting his general feeling that the BBC senior management paid little attention stating: "I can\'t remember ever having a serious conversation with anyone above me in the BBC about Radio 3 ... I would much rather have had the feeling that they thought it mattered what Radio 3 did."<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>328\xe2\x80\x93329</span></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Henry-purcell.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Henry-purcell.jpg/220px-Henry-purcell.jpg" width="220" height="280" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Henry-purcell.jpg/330px-Henry-purcell.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Henry-purcell.jpg/440px-Henry-purcell.jpg 2x" data-file-width="470" data-file-height="599" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Henry-purcell.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The tercentenary of Henry Purcell\'s death was marked in 1995 by the award-winning Radio 3 series <i>Fairest Isle</i></div></div></div>\n<p>Drummond\'s successor was <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Kenyon" title="Nicholas Kenyon">Nicholas Kenyon</a>, previously chief music critic of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">The Observer</a></i>, who took over in February 1992 and was immediately faced with the looming launch date for commercial competitor <a href="/wiki/Classic_FM_(UK)" title="Classic FM (UK)">Classic FM</a> who were, and still remain, Radio 3\'s biggest rivals. Kenyon, similar to <a href="/wiki/Aubrey_Singer" title="Aubrey Singer">Singer</a> a decade earlier, believed that Radio 3 had to make changes to its presentation before the new station began broadcasting rather than react later.<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>304, 339</span></sup> As a result, three senior producers were sent to study classical music stations in the United States<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>339</span></sup> and the station hired advertising agents <a href="/wiki/Saatchi_%26_Saatchi" title="Saatchi &amp; Saatchi">Saatchi &amp; Saatchi</a> to help improve public perception. Kenyon\'s tenure was to meet with much controversy: in attempts to update the station\'s presentation, popular announcers <a href="/w/index.php?title=Malcolm_Ruthven&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Malcolm Ruthven (page does not exist)">Malcolm Ruthven</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Peter_Barker_(announcer)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Peter Barker (announcer) (page does not exist)">Peter Barker</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tony_Scotland&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tony Scotland (page does not exist)">Tony Scotland</a> were axed; drama was cut by a quarter resulting in a letter of protest to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> signed by <a href="/wiki/Harold_Pinter" title="Harold Pinter">Harold Pinter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Stoppard" title="Tom Stoppard">Tom Stoppard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fay_Weldon" title="Fay Weldon">Fay Weldon</a> among others;<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>342</span></sup> two new programmes for drive time, entitled <i>On Air</i> and <i>In Tune</i>, were launched<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>341</span></sup> and a new three-hour programme of popular classics on Sunday mornings fronted by <a href="/wiki/Brian_Kay" title="Brian Kay">Brian Kay</a> was also launched.<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>342</span></sup>\n</p><p>These moves were defended by Kenyon who argued that the changes were not "some ghastly descent into populism" but were instead to create "access points" for new listeners.<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>341</span></sup> However, there was still "widespread disbelief"<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>357</span></sup> when it was announced in the summer that a new morning programme would take the 9<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>pm spot from the revered <i><a href="/wiki/Composer_of_the_Week" title="Composer of the Week">Composer of the Week</a></i> and would be presented by a signing from Classic FM \xe2\x80\x93 the disc jockey <a href="/wiki/Paul_Gambaccini" title="Paul Gambaccini">Paul Gambaccini</a>. The criticism, especially once the programme went on air a few weeks later, was so unrelenting that Gambaccini announced the following spring that he would not be renewing his contract with Radio 3.<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>357</span></sup>\n</p><p>However, Kenyon\'s controllership was marked by several highly distinguished programming successes. <i>Fairest Isle</i> was an ambitious project from 1995 which marked the 300th anniversary of the death of <a href="/wiki/Henry_Purcell" title="Henry Purcell">Henry Purcell</a> with a year-long celebration of British music and the programme <i>Sounding the Century</i>, which ran for two years from 1997, presented a retrospective of 20th-century music. Both won awards.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\nHe also introduced a number of well received specialist programmes including children\'s programme <i>The Music Machine</i>, early music programme <i>Spirit of the Age</i>, jazz showcase <i>Impressions</i>, vocal music programme <i>Voices</i> and the arts programme <i><a href="/wiki/Night_Waves" title="Night Waves">Night Waves</a></i>.\n</p><p>BBC Radio 3 began nighttime transmissions in 1996 with the introduction of <i><a href="/wiki/Euroclassic_Notturno" title="Euroclassic Notturno">Through the Night</a></i>, consisting of radio recordings from members of the <a href="/wiki/European_Broadcasting_Union" title="European Broadcasting Union">European Broadcasting Union</a> and distributed to some of these other stations under the title <i>Euroclassic Notturno</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The introduction of 24-hour broadcasting resulted in the introduction of a 22.00 fixed programming point so that if live programme overran, later programming could be cancelled to allow <i>Through the Night</i> to begin promptly.\n</p><p>In 1998, <a href="/wiki/Roger_Wright_(music_administrator)" title="Roger Wright (music administrator)">Roger Wright</a> took over as controller of the station. Soon after his appointment some changes were made to showcase a wider variety of music; a new, relaxed, late-night music programme <i><a href="/wiki/Late_Junction" title="Late Junction">Late Junction</a></i> featured a wide variety of genres; programmes focusing on jazz and world music were given a higher profile as were programmes presented by <a href="/wiki/Brian_Kay" title="Brian Kay">Brian Kay</a>, focusing on light music, and <a href="/wiki/Andy_Kershaw" title="Andy Kershaw">Andy Kershaw</a>, whose show was previously dropped by Radio 1. In these changes, Wright believed that, in the case of the former, he was addressing "this feeling people had that they didn\'t want to put Radio 3 on unless they were going to listen carefully"<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and in the latter cases that he was "not <a href="/wiki/Dumbing_down" title="Dumbing down">dumbing down</a> but smarting up" the programmes.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BBC_Radio_3.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/43/BBC_Radio_3.png/220px-BBC_Radio_3.png" width="220" height="105" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/4/43/BBC_Radio_3.png 1.5x" data-file-width="296" data-file-height="141" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BBC_Radio_3.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The BBC Radio 3 logo, 2000\xe2\x80\x932007</div></div></div>\n<p>By 2004, Radio 3\'s programming and services were being recognised by the corporation at large, as seen in the 2003/4 Charter renewal application and the Annual report for the year which reported that Radio 3 had "achieved a record [audience] reach in the first quarter of 2004",<sup id="cite_ref-AR34_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR34-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> and by the government: the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_(United_Kingdom)" title="Secretary of State (United Kingdom)">Secretary of State\'s</a> foreword to the government\'s <a href="/wiki/Green_Paper" class="mw-redirect" title="Green Paper">Green Paper</a> in 2005 made special mention of "the sort of commitment to new talent that has made Radio 3 the largest commissioner of new music in the world" as a model for what the BBC should be about.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By 2008 however, the station faced pressures to increase its audience by making programmes more accessible while loyal listeners began to complain about the tone of these new changes. Presentation was described as "gruesome in tone and level"<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> and global music output was mocked as "street-smart fusions" and "global pop".<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> At the same time <a href="/wiki/RAJAR" title="RAJAR">RAJAR</a> began to record lower listening figures and decisions on policy were being changed resulting in the children\'s programme <i>Making Tracks</i>, experimental music programme <i><a href="/wiki/Mixing_It" title="Mixing It">Mixing It</a></i>, theatre and film programme <i>Stage and Screen</i> and <i>Brian Kay\'s Light Programme</i> all being dropped, a reduction in the number of concerts<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> and format changes to several other programmes. In spite of the changes, figures still continued to fall.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:260px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ninth_Symphony_original.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3f/Ninth_Symphony_original.png" width="258" height="201" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="258" data-file-height="201" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ninth_Symphony_original.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Beethoven Experience: A manuscript page of Beethoven\'s Ninth Symphony.</div></div></div>\n<p>The mid to late 2000s did however offer new projects undertaken on the station: <i>The <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_van_Beethoven" title="Ludwig van Beethoven">Beethoven</a> Experience</i> in June 2005 saw the broadcast of his works broadcast non-stop for six days.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> A similar project occurred six months later when <i>A <a href="/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach" title="Johann Sebastian Bach">Bach</a> Christmas</i> was run for ten days in the lead to Christmas<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> and in February 2007 when a week was similarly given over to the works of <a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Ilyich_Tchaikovsky" title="Pyotr Ilyich Tchaikovsky">Tchaikovsky</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Igor_Stravinsky" title="Igor Stravinsky">Stravinsky</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Schubert" class="mw-redirect" title="Schubert">Schubert</a> in March 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> As part of the original Beethoven Experience, the BBC trialled its first music downloads over the internet by offering free music downloads of all nine symphonies as played by the BBC Philharmonic Orchestra under <a href="/wiki/Gianandrea_Noseda" title="Gianandrea Noseda">Gianandrea Noseda</a>. The stated aim was "to gauge audiences\' appetite for music downloads and their preferred content, and will inform the development of the BBC strategy for audio downloads and on demand content".<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The experiment was wildly successful, attracting 1.4 million downloads but was met with anger from the major classical record labels who considered it unfair competition and "devaluing the perceived value of music".<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> As a result, no further free downloads have been offered, including as part of the <a href="/wiki/BBC_iPlayer" title="BBC iPlayer">BBC iPlayer</a> service, and the BBC Trust has ruled out any classical music podcasts with extracts longer than one minute.\n</p><p>In 2007, Radio 3 also began to experiment with a visual broadcast as well as the audio transmissions. In October 2007, Radio 3 collaborated with <a href="/wiki/English_National_Opera" title="English National Opera">English National Opera</a> in presenting a live video stream of a performance of <a href="/wiki/Carmen" title="Carmen">Carmen</a>, "the first time a UK opera house has offered a complete production online"<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> and in September 2008, Radio 3 launched a filmed series of concerts that was available to watch live and on demand for seven days "in high quality vision".<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> This strategy was also introduced to some of the BBC Proms concerts.\n</p><p>By the latter years of the 2000s, Radio 3\'s prospects were improving. The year 2008/9 saw the introduction of more concerts<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> and other innovations had introduced Radio 3\'s largest event to a wider audience. The introduction of family orientated concerts to the <a href="/wiki/The_Proms" title="The Proms">BBC Proms</a>, which are broadcast live on Radio 3, helped the station to introduce itself to a younger audience. Innovations of this type began in 2008 with the introduction of a concert celebrating the music from the television programme <i><a href="/wiki/Doctor_Who" title="Doctor Who">Doctor Who</a></i> as composed by <a href="/wiki/Murray_Gold" title="Murray Gold">Murray Gold</a><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> and was later followed by a further Doctor Who prom in 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-DrWho2010_prom_R3Blog_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DrWho2010_prom_R3Blog-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> a free family prom in 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> another free <i><a href="/wiki/Horrible_Histories_(2009_TV_series)" title="Horrible Histories (2009 TV series)">Horrible Histories</a></i> prom in 2011<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> and a <a href="/wiki/Wallace_and_Gromit" title="Wallace and Gromit">Wallace and Gromit</a> prom in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> These particular concerts were introduced by Wright, who became Proms Director in addition to his duties at Radio 3 in October 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> and many were also televised for broadcast at a later date. The mix in these proms of classical music to combine with music of a classical nature from the programmes was hoped to introduce a much younger audience to the genres catered for by Radio 3.<sup id="cite_ref-DrWho2010_prom_R3Blog_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DrWho2010_prom_R3Blog-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BBC_Radio_3_live_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/BBC_Radio_3_live_2016.jpg/220px-BBC_Radio_3_live_2016.jpg" width="220" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/BBC_Radio_3_live_2016.jpg/330px-BBC_Radio_3_live_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/BBC_Radio_3_live_2016.jpg/440px-BBC_Radio_3_live_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3588" data-file-height="1841" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BBC_Radio_3_live_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>BBC Radio 3 broadcasting live from the <a href="/wiki/Southbank_Centre" title="Southbank Centre">Southbank Centre</a> in 2016</div></div></div>\n<p>As of  2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> Radio 3 was having to undergo further changes as a result of recent findings from the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Trust" title="BBC Trust">BBC Trust</a>. In the station\'s latest service review, carried out in 2010, the Trust recommended the station become more accessible to new audiences, easier to navigate through the different genres and to review the output of the BBC\'s orchestras and singers.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Soon after this verdict, the license fee was capped and the BBC given more services to pay for with the same level of income. As a result, the corporation had to reduce its costs. In the proposal entitled <i>Delivering Quality First</i>, the BBC proposed that Radio 3 contribute by broadcasting 25% fewer live or specially recorded lunchtime concerts and reducing the number of specially recorded evening concerts.<sup id="cite_ref-DQF_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DQF-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The Trust did recognise however that "Radio 3 plays a vital role in the cultural and creative life of the UK"<sup id="cite_ref-DQF_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DQF-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> and as a result, the report did agree to reinvest in the Proms,<sup id="cite_ref-DQF_46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DQF-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> to retain the long dramas found on the station<sup id="cite_ref-DQF_46-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DQF-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> and to continue to broadcast a new concert live each evening.<sup id="cite_ref-DQF_46-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DQF-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operation">Operation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Operation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Broadcasting_House_and_East_Wing.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Broadcasting_House_and_East_Wing.jpg/250px-Broadcasting_House_and_East_Wing.jpg" width="250" height="335" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Broadcasting_House_and_East_Wing.jpg/375px-Broadcasting_House_and_East_Wing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Broadcasting_House_and_East_Wing.jpg/500px-Broadcasting_House_and_East_Wing.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1918" data-file-height="2568" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Broadcasting_House_and_East_Wing.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>BBC Radio 3\'s studios are located in Broadcasting House, London.</div></div></div>\n<p>BBC Radio 3 broadcasts from studios inside the 1930s wing of <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting_House" title="Broadcasting House">Broadcasting House</a> in central <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>. However, in addition to these studios, certain programmes and performances are broadcast from other BBC bases including from <a href="/wiki/BBC_Cymru_Wales" title="BBC Cymru Wales">BBC Cymru Wales</a>\' <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a> headquarters and <a href="/wiki/BBC_North" title="BBC North">BBC North</a>\'s headquarters at <a href="/wiki/MediaCityUK" title="MediaCityUK">MediaCityUK</a>, Salford.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The BBC also has recording facilities at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Festival_Hall" title="Royal Festival Hall">Royal Festival Hall</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_Hall" title="Queen Elizabeth Hall">Queen Elizabeth Hall</a> which can be used to record and broadcast performances at these venues.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Properties_FOI_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Properties_FOI-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>BBC Radio 3 is broadcast on the <a href="/wiki/FM_broadcasting" title="FM broadcasting">FM</a> band between 90.2 and 92.6 <a href="/wiki/Hertz" title="Hertz">MHz</a>, on <a href="/wiki/Digital_Audio_Broadcasting" class="mw-redirect" title="Digital Audio Broadcasting">DAB Digital Radio</a>, the digital television services <a href="/wiki/Freeview_(UK)" title="Freeview (UK)">Freeview</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freesat" title="Freesat">Freesat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sky_(UK_and_Ireland)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sky (UK and Ireland)">Sky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Media" title="Virgin Media">Virgin Media</a>, <a href="/wiki/TalkTalk_TV" title="TalkTalk TV">TalkTalk TV</a> and <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Media_Ireland" title="Virgin Media Ireland">Virgin Media Ireland</a>. Radio 3 programmes can be listened to live on the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Online" title="BBC Online">Radio 3 Website</a> through the RadioPlayer and <a href="/wiki/BBC_iPlayer" title="BBC iPlayer">BBC iPlayer</a> services; the iPlayer also allows Radio 3 programmes to be heard for 30 days after broadcast.\n</p><p>On its FM frequencies, the station uses less <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_range_compression" title="Dynamic range compression">dynamic range compression</a> of the volume of music than rival station <a href="/wiki/Classic_FM_(UK)" title="Classic FM (UK)">Classic FM</a>. On DAB it uses dynamic range control (DRC) which allows compression to be defined by the user.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The station also uses a BBC-designed <a href="/wiki/Pulse_code_modulation" class="mw-redirect" title="Pulse code modulation">pulse code modulation</a> digitisation technique similar to <a href="/wiki/NICAM" title="NICAM">NICAM</a>, which is used for outside broadcasts running through a telephone line. This runs at a sample rate of 14,000 per second per channel.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> A similar technique was later used for recording at the same rate. In September 2010, for the final week of the Proms broadcasts, the BBC trialled XHQ (Extra High Quality), a live <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a> stream transmitted at a rate of 320<a href="/wiki/Kilobit" title="Kilobit">kbit</a>/s, instead of Radio 3\'s usual 192kbit/s, using its AAC-LC \'Coyopa\' coding technology.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> This technology was later developed further, and Radio 3 became the first BBC Radio station to broadcast permanently in this High Definition Sound (as it has been termed) format.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_programmes">Notable programmes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Notable programmes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Choral_Evensong"><i>Choral Evensong</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Choral Evensong">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Choral_Evensong_(BBC)" title="Choral Evensong (BBC)">Choral Evensong (BBC)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:187px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Westminster_abbey_west.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Westminster_abbey_west.jpg/185px-Westminster_abbey_west.jpg" width="185" height="247" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Westminster_abbey_west.jpg/278px-Westminster_abbey_west.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Westminster_abbey_west.jpg/370px-Westminster_abbey_west.jpg 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Westminster_abbey_west.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The first BBC broadcast of <i>Choral Evensong</i> came from Westminster Abbey in 1926</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglican</a> service of sung <a href="/wiki/Evening_Prayer_(Anglican)" title="Evening Prayer (Anglican)">evening prayer</a> is broadcast every Wednesday at 3:30pm during the <i>Afternoon Concerts</i> block on Radio 3 live from cathedrals, university college chapels and churches throughout the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-Choral_evensong_programme_page_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Choral_evensong_programme_page-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> On occasion, it broadcasts <a href="/wiki/Vespers" title="Vespers">Choral Vespers</a> from <a href="/wiki/Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholicism">Catholic</a> cathedrals, (such as <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Cathedral" title="Westminster Cathedral">Westminster Cathedral</a>), Orthodox Vespers, or a recorded service from choral foundations abroad. <i>Choral Evensong</i> is the BBC\'s longest-running outside broadcast programme, the first edition having been relayed from <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey" title="Westminster Abbey">Westminster Abbey</a> on 7 October 1926.<sup id="cite_ref-Choral_evensong_programme_page_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Choral_evensong_programme_page-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Its 80th anniversary was celebrated, also live from Westminster Abbey, with a service on 11 October 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When <i>Choral Evensong</i> was moved from Radio 4 to Radio 3 with effect from 8 April 1970 and reduced to just one broadcast per month, the BBC received 2,500 letters of complaint, and weekly transmissions were resumed on 1 July.<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>262\xe2\x80\x93263</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-move1970_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-move1970-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2007 the live broadcast was switched to Sundays, which again caused protests.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The live transmission was returned to Wednesdays in September 2008, with a recorded repeat on Sunday afternoons in approximately the same time. <i>Choral Evensong</i> forms part of Radio 3\'s remit on religious programming though non-religious listeners have campaigned for its retention.<sup id="cite_ref-move1970_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-move1970-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Composer_of_the_Week"><i>Composer of the Week</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Composer of the Week">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/Composer_of_the_Week" title="Composer of the Week">Composer of the Week</a></i> was launched in the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Home_Service" title="BBC Home Service">BBC Home Service</a> on 2 August 1943 under its original title of <i>This Week\'s Composer</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Donovan_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Donovan-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> From 15 December 1964 the programme became a regular feature in the schedule of the newly established daytime "Third Network" classical music service, the Music Programme (later to be absorbed into Radio 3).<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>231</span></sup> The programme was renamed <i>Composer of the Week</i> on 18 January 1988.\n</p><p>Each week, in five daily programmes, which air at midday, the work of a particular composer is studied in detail and illustrated with musical excerpts. <a href="/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach" title="Johann Sebastian Bach">Bach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_van_Beethoven" title="Ludwig van Beethoven">Beethoven</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Haydn" title="Joseph Haydn">Haydn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">Mozart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Handel" class="mw-redirect" title="Handel">Handel</a> have all featured once most years,<sup id="cite_ref-Donovan_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Donovan-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> a different aspect of their work being chosen for study each time. However, the programme also covers more \'difficult\' or less-widely known composers, with weeks devoted to <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Rubbra" title="Edmund Rubbra">Rubbra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Medtner" title="Nikolai Medtner">Medtner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Havergal_Brian" title="Havergal Brian">Havergal Brian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vitezslava_Kapralova" class="mw-redirect" title="Vitezslava Kapralova">Kapralova</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Minimalist_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Minimalist music">Minimalists</a> among others. The programme is written and presented by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Donald_Macleod_(Radio_3_presenter)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Donald Macleod (Radio 3 presenter) (page does not exist)">Donald Macleod</a>. On 2 August 2013, in honour of the station\'s 70th year, listeners were asked to nominate a composer who had never before been featured for a special broadcast at Christmas.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The composer listeners chose was <a href="/wiki/Louise_Farrenc" title="Louise Farrenc">Louise Farrenc</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Lunchtime_.2F_Afternoon_Concerts"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Lunchtime_/_Afternoon_Concerts"><i>Lunchtime / Afternoon Concerts</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Lunchtime / Afternoon Concerts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>These two programs showcase live or recorded performances from venues across the country. <i>Lunchtime</i> is from 1<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>to 2<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>pm and <i>Afternoon</i> is later on until 5 with presenters being rotated weekly for the latter program. The live Monday edition of <i>Lunchtime</i> is repeated on Sunday at the same time.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Record_Review"><i>Record Review</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Record Review">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><i>Record Review</i> is a Saturday morning programme (usually airing from 9<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>am to 12:15<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>pm) dealing with recent classical music releases, topical issues and interviews. The programme title is a return of <i>Record Review</i> which was broadcast on Network Three occasionally from 1949, then weekly from 1957 presented by John Lade and then from 1981, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Vaughan" title="Paul Vaughan">Paul Vaughan</a>, until 1998. From 1998-2015 it became <i>CD Review</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> with the format remaining largely the same. Then, from 2 January 2016, its title reverted to <i>Record Review</i> to reflect the diversity of media proliferating (CDs, downloads, streaming, and so forth). It includes the feature <i>Building a Library</i> which surveys and recommends available recordings of specific works. In 2006 <i>Building a Library</i> was attacked as \'elitist\' for including such composers as <a href="/wiki/Karl_Amadeus_Hartmann" title="Karl Amadeus Hartmann">Karl Amadeus Hartmann</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elliott_Carter" title="Elliott Carter">Elliott Carter</a> and lesser-known works of great composers, at the expense of well-known mainstream works.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> However, the charge was rebutted by the programme\'s producer, Mark Lowther, who said that Radio 3 audiences wanted programmes that challenged and inspired.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> As of  2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> the regular presenter of <i>Record Review</i> is Andrew McGregor.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jazz_Record_Requests"><i>Jazz Record Requests</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Jazz Record Requests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><i>Jazz Record Requests</i> was the first weekly jazz programme on the Third Programme. First presented by the jazz musician <a href="/wiki/Humphrey_Lyttelton" title="Humphrey Lyttelton">Humphrey Lyttelton</a>, the 30-minute programme was launched in December 1964 and is still running. Now an hour long, it is still broadcast on Saturday, usually in the late afternoon. Presenters on Radio 3 have included <a href="/wiki/Steve_Race" title="Steve Race">Steve Race</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Clayton" title="Peter Clayton">Peter Clayton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Fox_(jazz_critic)" title="Charles Fox (jazz critic)">Charles Fox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Smith_(radio_presenter)" title="Geoffrey Smith (radio presenter)">Geoffrey Smith</a>. <a href="/wiki/Alyn_Shipton" title="Alyn Shipton">Alyn Shipton</a> became the presenter in May 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pied_Piper"><i>Pied Piper</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Pied Piper">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><i>Pied Piper</i> was an iconic children\'s programme, presented by early music specialist, <a href="/wiki/David_Munrow" title="David Munrow">David Munrow</a>, it had the sub-title Tales and Music for Younger Listeners<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>265</span></sup> and ran from August 1971 until 1976. Lively and varied, it was aimed at the 6\xe2\x80\x9312 age group, though  much older children and adults also listened.<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>266</span></sup> The programme ran for five series and a total of 655 episodes until it was brought to an end by Munrow\'s untimely death in May 1976.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_3_in_Concert"><i>Radio 3 in Concert</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Radio 3 in Concert">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><i>Radio 3 in Concert</i> (originally <i>Live in Concert</i>) is a weeknight programme, broadcast between 7:30 and 10<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>pm, with recorded concerts from various venues around the country and Europe. Regular presenters include Nicola Heywood Thomas, Martin Handley and <a href="/wiki/Petroc_Trelawny" title="Petroc Trelawny">Petroc Trelawny</a>. The last broadcast with the <i>Live in Concert</i> name was in 15 July 2015.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Early_Music_Show"><i>The Early Music Show</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: The Early Music Show">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/programmes/b006tn49"><i>The Early Music Show</i></a> is broadcast at 2<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>pm each Sunday which presents European music from the time of Bach and earlier. Episodes cover the music itself as well as performers and occasional discussions of musical style.  Regular presenters include <a href="/wiki/Lucie_Skeaping" title="Lucie Skeaping">Lucie Skeaping</a> and Hannah French.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Through_the_Night"><i>Through the Night</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Through the Night">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The show broadcasts for 6 hours, beginning weekdays at 0:30 and weekends at 1 in the morning. It currently has three regular presenters: Catriona Young, John Shea and Jonathan Swain. The show is a spin-off version of <a href="/wiki/Euroclassic_Notturno" title="Euroclassic Notturno">Euroclassic Notturno</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="News_broadcasts">News broadcasts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: News broadcasts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>BBC Radio 3\'s remit focuses mainly on music and the arts, and news is a minor part of its output, though the station does provide concise news bulletins throughout the <i>Breakfast</i> programme and also at 1<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>pm, 5<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>pm and 6<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>pm to give listeners the chance to switch to a more news-oriented station should they want more details about a particular news item.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Following the <i>Delivering Quality First</i> proposals, it was suggested that Radio 3 share bulletins with Radio 4, so that the same bulletins would be broadcast on both channels.<sup id="cite_ref-DQF_46-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DQF-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> During weekdays the 1<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>pm,  5<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>pm and 6<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>pm news bulletins are read by a member of the Radio 4 presentation team.\n</p><p>As of  2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> the Radio 3 Breakfast newsreading team included Viji Alles, Chris Berrow, <a href="/wiki/Kathy_Clugston" title="Kathy Clugston">Kathy Clugston</a>, Mark Forrest, Jill Anderson, Debbie Russ, John Shea, <a href="/wiki/Susan_Rae" title="Susan Rae">Susan Rae</a>, Paul Guinery.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Source only mentions one newsreader (Paul Guinery) and is dated 2011... (February 2018)">additional citation(s) needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> These newsreaders can be heard on the <i>Breakfast</i> programme and at 1&#160;pm on weekends.\n</p><p>David McNeil, originally from <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, was a foreign correspondent for the BBC for 21 years, based in <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johannesburg" title="Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> and <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington</a>. He reported for the BBC from forty-six countries and also presented news programmes on BBC Radio.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> He was a news presenter on Radio 3 until his retirement on 27 March 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Performing_groups">Performing groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Performing groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/BBC_Orchestras_and_Singers" title="BBC Orchestras and Singers">BBC Orchestras and Singers</a></div>\n<p>Much of Radio 3\'s orchestral output is sourced from the BBC\'s Orchestras and Singers. These groups are:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/BBC_Symphony_Orchestra" title="BBC Symphony Orchestra">BBC Symphony Orchestra</a> and <a href="/wiki/BBC_Symphony_Chorus" title="BBC Symphony Chorus">Symphony Chorus</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/BBC_Concert_Orchestra" title="BBC Concert Orchestra">BBC Concert Orchestra</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Watford" title="Watford">Watford</a></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/BBC_Philharmonic" title="BBC Philharmonic">BBC Philharmonic</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/City_of_Salford" title="City of Salford">Salford</a></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/BBC_National_Orchestra_of_Wales" title="BBC National Orchestra of Wales">BBC National Orchestra of Wales</a> and the BBC National Chorus of Wales, based in <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/BBC_Scottish_Symphony_Orchestra" title="BBC Scottish Symphony Orchestra">BBC Scottish Symphony Orchestra</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/BBC_Singers" title="BBC Singers">BBC Singers</a>, based in London.</li></ul>\n<p>In addition to the BBC\'s own orchestras it also has broadcast commitments to the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Big_Band" title="BBC Big Band">BBC Big Band</a>, which is externally managed, and also broadcasts some works of the <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Orchestra" title="Ulster Orchestra">Ulster Orchestra</a>, which it part funds.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controllers">Controllers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Controllers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>1967\xe2\x80\x931971 <b><a href="/wiki/P._H._Newby" title="P. H. Newby">Howard Newby</a></b></li></ul>\n<dl><dd>An author, he published four novels during his time at the Third Programme/Radio 3, winning the first <a href="/wiki/Man_Booker_Prize" class="mw-redirect" title="Man Booker Prize">Booker Prize</a> for fiction in 1969. Oversaw the implementation of <i>Broadcasting in the Seventies</i> and an increase in the amount of classical music on Radio 3.<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>253</span></sup></dd></dl>\n<ul><li>1972\xe2\x80\x931978 <b><a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hearst" title="Stephen Hearst">Stephen Hearst</a></b></li></ul>\n<dl><dd>Previously head of BBC\'s television music and arts department, Hearst attempted to make Radio 3 more accessible to a wider audience by introducing drivetime and request programmes as well as themed weekends. Some of these ventures were poorly viewed by critics.<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>289, 296</span></sup></dd></dl>\n<ul><li>1979\xe2\x80\x931987 <b><a href="/wiki/Ian_McIntyre" title="Ian McIntyre">Ian McIntyre</a></b></li></ul>\n<dl><dd>Previously controller of Radio 4, McIntyre faced budgetary cuts that closed several orchestras and uncomfortable relations with the Music Division.<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>302</span></sup> The possibility of future competition to Radio 3 also resulted in more programmes viewed as populist by critics in an attempt to retain listeners.<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>304</span></sup></dd></dl>\n<ul><li>1987\xe2\x80\x931992 <b><a href="/wiki/John_Drummond_(arts_administrator)" title="John Drummond (arts administrator)">John Drummond</a></b></li></ul>\n<dl><dd>Previously an administrator for events including the <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Edinburgh Festival">Edinburgh Festival</a>, Drummond introduced repeats of classic drama performances and celebrations of artists anniversaries. His work also included programmes targeting fringe genres and ambitious outside broadcasts.</dd></dl>\n<ul><li>1992\xe2\x80\x931998 <b><a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Kenyon" title="Nicholas Kenyon">Nicholas Kenyon</a></b></li></ul>\n<dl><dd>Kenyon, previously chief music critic of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">The Observer</a></i>, made many controversial decisions relating to accessibility to the service in light of the launch of Classic FM including new drive time programmes. However several celebrated programmes and series of programmes were launched and Radio 3 began 24-hour broadcasting.</dd></dl>\n<ul><li>1998\xe2\x80\x932014 <b><a href="/wiki/Roger_Wright_(music_administrator)" title="Roger Wright (music administrator)">Roger Wright</a></b></li></ul>\n<dl><dd>Wright attempted to ensure that all of the station\'s musical genres were represented more equitably, and to "smarten up" programmes. While some of these measures were recognised by the BBC and Government, the audience began to decrease, and attempts by Wright to make programmes more accessible were met with complaints from listeners.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> It was announced in March 2014 that Wright would step down in early September 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<ul><li>2015\xe2\x80\x93present <b><a href="/wiki/Alan_Davey_(civil_servant)" title="Alan Davey (civil servant)">Alan Davey</a></b></li></ul>\n<dl><dd>Davey became Controller in January 2015, having been chief executive of <a href="/wiki/Arts_Council_England" title="Arts Council England">Arts Council England</a> since 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy">Controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Controller Nicholas Kenyon summed up the perennial problem of Radio 3 as "the tension between highbrow culture and popular appeal \xe2\x80\xa6the cost of what we do and the number of people who make use of it":<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>364</span></sup> elitism versus populism (or \'dumbing down\') and the question of cost per listener. This argument has included members of the BBC, listeners and several different protest groups.\n</p><p>In 1969, two hundred members of the BBC staff protested to the director general at changes which would \'emasculate\' Radio 3, while managing director of radio <a href="/wiki/Ian_Trethowan" title="Ian Trethowan">Ian Trethowan</a> described the station in a memorandum as "a private playground for elitists to indulge in cerebral masturbation".<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>255</span></sup> Later, former Radio 3 controller John Drummond complained that the senior ranks of the BBC took no interest in what he was doing.<sup id="cite_ref-Drummond365_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Drummond365-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1995/6 listeners and press critics protested against the introduction into a slot formerly used for <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_3#Composer_of_the_Week" title="BBC Radio 3">Composer of the Week</a> of a programme presented by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Gambaccini" title="Paul Gambaccini">Paul Gambaccini</a>, a former <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1" title="BBC Radio 1">Radio 1</a> and <a href="/wiki/Classic_FM_(UK)" title="Classic FM (UK)">Classic FM</a> presenter. This was seen as part of a wider move towards popularisation, to compete with Classic FM and to increase ratings.<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>357\xe2\x80\x93358</span></sup> Gambaccini is quoted as saying: "I had a specific mission to invite [Radio 4\'s] Today listeners to stay with the BBC rather than go to Classic FM."<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Several groups were formed to protest against any changes to the station. These have included:\n</p>\n<ul><li><b>The Third Programme Defence Society</b> (1957) opposed cuts in broadcasting hours and the removal of what the BBC considered "too difficult and too highbrow". Supported by <a href="/wiki/TS_Eliot" class="mw-redirect" title="TS Eliot">TS Eliot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Vaughan_Williams" title="Ralph Vaughan Williams">Ralph Vaughan Williams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Olivier" title="Laurence Olivier">Laurence Olivier</a><sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>169\xe2\x80\x93174</span></sup></li>\n<li><b>The Campaign for Better Broadcasting</b> (1969) opposed proposed cuts in Radio 3\'s speech output. Supported by <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Boult" title="Adrian Boult">Sir Adrian Boult</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Miller" title="Jonathan Miller">Jonathan Miller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Moore" title="Henry Moore">Henry Moore</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Melly" title="George Melly">George Melly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Envy1996_8-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Envy1996-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>255\xe2\x80\x93257</span></sup></li>\n<li><b><a href="/w/index.php?title=Friends_of_Radio_3&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Friends of Radio 3 (page does not exist)">Friends of Radio 3</a></b> (FoR3),<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> a listeners\' campaign group set up in 2003 to express concern at changes to the station\'s style<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> and scheduling, including the shift to presenter-led programmes stripped through the week, as on Classic FM and other commercial music stations. Officially, the BBC stated that "the network\'s target audience has been redefined and broadened and the schedule began to be recast to move towards this during 1999."<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The group\'s stated aim is "To engage with the BBC, to question the policies which depart from Radio 3\'s remit to deliver a high quality programme of classical music, spoken arts and thought, and to convey listener concerns to BBC management." The group is supported by <a href="/wiki/Gillian_Weir" title="Gillian Weir">Dame Gillian Weir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robin_Holloway" title="Robin Holloway">Robin Holloway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Motion" title="Andrew Motion">Andrew Motion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Drabble" title="Margaret Drabble">Dame Margaret Drabble</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The BBC has  rejected claims that the network has \'dumbed down\'.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_BBC_radio_stations" title="List of BBC radio stations">List of BBC radio stations</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_Radio_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-BBC_Radio_3_Service_Licence-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-BBC_Radio_3_Service_Licence_1-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/bbctrust/our_work/services/radio/service_licences/bbc_radio_3.html">"BBC Radio 3"</a>. <i>Service Licences</i>. Classic FM uses it.  BBC Radio 3 (in deference to hi-fi listeners) does not use it in the evening.  Rock/pop/etc-music stations use it all the time." and regarding DAB "Classic FM apply some processing to their audio signal, which may vary from programme to programme.  BBC Radio 3 and BBC Radio 4 do not apply processing but, in the digital signal, offer dynamic range control (DRC) which gives the listener the option of switching to a compressed form of the audio at the receiver."</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-50"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-50">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/blogs/bbcinternet/2010/09/bbc_proms_extra_high_quality_audio.html">BBC Internet blog</a> (search that page for "dynamic range" to find several people have observed <b>some</b> compression being applied to Radio 3\'s FM signal even in the evenings, but not as much as Classic FM)</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-51"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-51">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/blogs/radiolabs/2009/10/what_happens_to_the_proms_afte.shtml">BBC Radio Labs</a> "The FM signal has dynamic range compression applied via an Optimod processor"  (note this discussion is about The Proms, which are broadcast during the evening, so the source above which said it isn\'t applied in the evening doesn\'t appear to be correct)</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-52"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-52">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.theguardian.com/technology/askjack+media/bbc">The Guardian: Ask Jack (BBC)</a> "The BBC\'s online iPlayer gives the best quality with Radio 3 for two reasons. First, it uses a higher-quality codec than the other digital systems. Second, it and does not have any dynamic range compression (DRC) ... On FM, Radio 3 uses DRC to reduce the dynamic range ... People vary in their sensitivity to ... the effects of DRC, so I\'m sympathetic to those who prefer FM to iPlayer, or vinyl to CD, or vice versa. However, an iPlayer signal should sound better if reproduced via the same hi-fi system."</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-53"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-53">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/blogs/bbcinternet/2010/09/bbc_proms_extra_high_quality_audio.html">"Listening to the Proms in Extra High Quality"</a>.
